  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_403fb602-e176-4985-800e-1ee95963a490'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3797516196270719731">At the end of <em>Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</em>, the powerful Dark wizard Gellert Grindelwald was captured in New York with the help of Newt Scamander. But, making good on his threat, Grindelwald escapes custody and sets about gathering followers, most unsuspecting of his true agenda: to raise pure-blood wizards up to rule over all non-magical beings.<br/><br/>In an effort to </span>
  <span id="freeText3797516196270719731" style="display:none">At the end of <em>Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</em>, the powerful Dark wizard Gellert Grindelwald was captured in New York with the help of Newt Scamander. But, making good on his threat, Grindelwald escapes custody and sets about gathering followers, most unsuspecting of his true agenda: to raise pure-blood wizards up to rule over all non-magical beings.<br /><br />In an effort to thwart Grindelwald’s plans, Albus Dumbledore enlists Newt, his former Hogwarts student, who agrees to help once again, unaware of the dangers that lie ahead. Lines are drawn as love and loyalty are tested, even among the truest friends and family, in an increasingly divided wizarding world.<br /><br />This second original screenplay from J.K. Rowling, illustrated with stunning line art from MinaLima, expands on earlier events that helped shaped the wizarding world, with some surprising nods to the Harry Potter stories that will delight fans of both the books and films.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1462633-if-i-read-the-book-then-i-can-say-i-read">If I read the book, then I can say I read the book. If I listen to the audio book, then I can say I have read the book. If you watch the movie, can you say that you have read the book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1462633'><a id="like_count_community_question_1462633" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1462633?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F39330961-fantastic-beasts---the-crimes-of-grindelwald">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1462633-if-i-read-the-book-then-i-can-say-i-read">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1462633-if-i-read-the-book-then-i-can-say-i-read">See all 8 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/65639595-adina"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/65639595-adina">Adina</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Definitely not. Have to agree with Enes F and Angelina here. If your only point of reference is the Harry Potter series, I can see how the question wo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Definitely not. Have to agree with Enes F and Angelina here. If your only point of reference is the Harry Potter series, I can see how the question would come up. For the most part, all of the HP movies follow the books in general. However, because you are taking a large book and cutting it down to a 2 hour movie there are obviously things that have to be left out and changes made by merging scenes or changing the characters making the statements/doing the actions. In my experience, most movies do not follow the books past the characters and part of the plot. Further, by only watching the movie you are not only missing out on the author's point of view, but also seeing what the directors and actors interpret and think will sell in a theater as opposed to what you would get out of the story by reading/listening to the book directly. To summarize: too much missing information and too many changes to consider watching a movie comparabable to reading/listening to the book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1471293-i-m-a-big-fan-of-harry-potter-in-general">I’m a big fan of “Harry Potter” in general and (to a slightly lesser degree), the first “Fantastic Beasts” (which I’ve read the screenplay of). However, I didn’t care much for “The Crimes of Grindelwald” (the film, that is). Should I read this, or just give it a miss? I’ll probably need the book for completion’s sake, but is it worth buying at full price, or just waiting until it’s cheaper?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/44014173-nicole">Nicole</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">My suggestion would be to read it even though you didn't like the film. I found that the book made things little clearer because everyone is named. Pl<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">My suggestion would be to read it even though you didn't like the film. I found that the book made things little clearer because everyone is named. Plus there was some things I didn't catch on to in the film. So the book was very helpful. Not everything is answered in this book, so it leaves you to wonder what the answer it. The story is more complex than her Harry Potter books. Read it, keep an open mind and know that we got 3 more films to answer everything.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_2343823057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343823057" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343823057?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408711705" href="/book/show/39337278-fantastic-beasts---the-crimes-of-grindelwald">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343823057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17936517333956215679"><b>Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Destroying Everything That Is Good about the Wizarding World</b><i> - A Guide in 10 Steps</i><br/><br/>It is likely that you have already seen the Fantastic Beasts sequel this week. I mean, we have waited two years for this, right? No point in waiting any longer. If you have not seen it, you might hold off from reading this review. It contains ALL the spoilers and might ruin the film for you. After seeing it two days ago, I left the movie theatre, not sure what to think. I was angry a</span>
  <span id="freeText17936517333956215679" style="display:none"><b>Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Destroying Everything That Is Good about the Wizarding World</b><i> - A Guide in 10 Steps</i><br /><br />It is likely that you have already seen the Fantastic Beasts sequel this week. I mean, we have waited two years for this, right? No point in waiting any longer. If you have not seen it, you might hold off from reading this review. It contains ALL the spoilers and might ruin the film for you. After seeing it two days ago, I left the movie theatre, not sure what to think. I was angry and disappointed but I could not say for what reason. Now I know. Here are the 10 reasons why <i>The Crimes of Grindelwald</i> is the worst film in the entire Potterverse:<br /><br /><b>1. More Magic Is Not The Answer to a Succesful Film</b><br />Remember how realistic and true the Wizarding World always seemed to be? It was right there, just out of reach. Hogwarts was definitely real, I was just too much of a muggle to see it. FB2 destroyed that illusion once and for all. The fragility that existed between these two worlds proved too weak to hold. FB2 is so magical and big and fantastic that the coexistence of muggles and wizards ceases to play a role. In Paris, it seems, you do not have to think about casting a spell in public. Muggles just won't notice that bloody big Chinese cat that runs around the city either.<br /><br /><b>2. Nagini</b><br />I definitely loved that character. But why was she in that film in the first place? There was no point in her being there. Apart from making this film seem more exciting that it is.<br /><br /><b>3. Queenie</b><br />My favourite character does not deserve to be treated this way. What the heck? Queenie becomes one of Grindelwald's closest allies because she does not want to live in a world where she cannot love a muggle. Makes total sense to change sides and hold tea parties with a tyrant and murderer. Cause when you have a man that loves you and a sister you love more than anything in the world and an ability to BLOODY READ MINDS, of course, you throw your common sense out of the window to support anarchy and chaos.<br /><br /><b>4. Leta Lestrange</b><br />Another fantastic character. Beautifully played by Zoë Kravitz. What a shame that she is no more than a tool to be killed off for dramatic effect. As the only black "main character", if that is what you want to call it, it seems kind of a dick move to eliminate her right away. By the way, have you noticed a pattern yet? We are only at Nr. 4 out of 10 and we already have three female characters treated like crap. You want more? I will give you more.<br /><br /><b>5. Mrs Lestrange</b><br />Leta's mother is another pawn and she gets the worst treatment of them all. As if rape and abuse are not enough, of course, she also has to die as soon as Leta was born, because that is all black or female characters seem to excel at in this film.<br />What is extremely illogical though, is how a random wizard can put an Imperius Curse on a woman that then just walks out of her house never to return...with no consequences? No husband trying to get her back? No investigations into what could have made her leave her family in just a nightgown? No one thinking of trying to find out whether someone literally put a spell on her? Bullshit.<br /><br /><b>6. Trying to Put Every Minor Character's Backstory in One Film</b><br />One of the things I loved about the Potter books was the fact that every character had their own history that could be glimpsed at sometimes, and usually was never fully revealed. Elaborate subplots are what added so much to these books. Of course, it was annoying not to see these side stories make it into the films. There was not enough room for them, not enough time. The films would have been 8 hours long otherwise (which I wouldn't have minded, anyway, but I do know it would have been impossible to do that). JKR tries to cram so much backstory in this film that it ruins the pacing and the expert storytelling. <br /><br /><b>7. Unnecessary and Unwanted Potter References</b><br />While we are talking about cramming things into this film, let's talk about Credence and the entirely ridiculous revelation that he is Dumbledore's brother. Not only is it a cheap trick in the fashion of <i>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</i>, where Voldemort suddenly has a daughter with Bellatrix Lestrange, it also does injustice to Harry's relationship with Dumbledore. Of course, we do not know everything about Dumbledore's past. But we thought the lying and hiding was finally over when Harry and Dumbledore met in the in-between in book 7. There were also signs that Ariana Dumbledore, his sister, might have been an Obscurial. You could also argue that the nature of Dumbledore's and Grindelwald's relationship was obvious. But for him to have yet another brother? I feel cheated on Harry's behalf AND on my own's.<br /><br /><b>8. Animation So Bad It Hurts My Eyes</b><br />How can a production with so much money suck so bad at making those shadowcats look real? What was that even?<br /><br /><b>9. Do We Really Need To Talk About Depp's Involvement In This Film?</b><br />Nope. Still stinks. You could almost say this film's suckiness is karma for casting him in the first place.<br /><br /><b>10. This Film is a Disgrace and an Insult to Every Potterhead</b><br />One of the few good things I take away from this film is that I have no desire whatsoever to buy any merch. I do not want the screenplay. I do not want the screenplay-to-film books. I do not want any Funkos or posters or artefacts. I do not want this film to exist in the first place.<br /><br />One last thing: I love Harry Potter more than anything. I am deeply in awe with J.K. Rowling for writing this outstanding series, for being outspoken, for opening so many doors for many YA authors and stories that would probably not exist otherwise. I have the deepest respect for her work. I have a freaking Deathly Hallows tattoo because I love this universe so much. It pains me to see something that I love so much go to ruins. I do not enjoy saying these things. I would rather write a positive review. I am holding on to the hope that this remains the worst of the films yet to be released and that they will return to being as good as the first Fantastic Beasts film. But at least I will not be surprised anymore when my hopes will fail to materialise.<br /><br /><b> I will respond to criticism and I do enjoy discussions. However, I will not accept hate or insults. Blocking people is fairly easy, so consider yourself warned.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17936517333956215679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2727855305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2727855305" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2727855305?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408711705" href="/book/show/39337278-fantastic-beasts---the-crimes-of-grindelwald">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2727855305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9719586168231222520"><b>3.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“DUMBLEDORE: Do you know why I admire you, Newt? More, perhaps, than any man I know? (off NEWT’S surprise) You don’t seek power or popularity. You simply ask, is the thing right in itself? If it is, then I must do it, no matter the cost.” </blockquote><br/><br/>Well well well. <b>Yet another money grab unnecessary book is yet again upon us...</b> one that I definitely bought because I'm a bitch for this useless-Harry-Potter-related-shit. This book literally took me <b>2 hours</b> to finish, which is, approximate</span>
  <span id="freeText9719586168231222520" style="display:none"><b>3.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“DUMBLEDORE: Do you know why I admire you, Newt? More, perhaps, than any man I know? (off NEWT’S surprise) You don’t seek power or popularity. You simply ask, is the thing right in itself? If it is, then I must do it, no matter the cost.” </blockquote><br /><br />Well well well. <b>Yet another money grab unnecessary book is yet again upon us...</b> one that I definitely bought because I'm a bitch for this useless-Harry-Potter-related-shit. This book literally took me <b>2 hours</b> to finish, which is, approximately, the duration of the movie. This is one of those books you read to expand your Goodreads total books score, and it makes you so satisfied to have finished 2 books in one day, as I have today. This book is made to make us feel good about our reading life. <b>Thx, book.</b> Well, this is not technically a book, but a movie script, and reviewing it feels more like <i>I'm reviewing the movie??? if that makes sense???</i> I'll just write some more general shit here. <br /><br /><i>At the end of Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them, the powerful Dark wizard Gellert Grindelwald was captured in New York with the help of Newt Scamander. But, making good on his threat, Grindelwald escapes custody and sets about gathering followers, most unsuspecting of his true agenda: to raise pure-blood wizards up to rule over all non-magical beings.<br /><br />In an effort to thwart Grindelwald’s plans, Albus Dumbledore enlists Newt, his former Hogwarts student, who agrees to help once again, unaware of the dangers that lie ahead. Lines are drawn as love and loyalty are tested, even among the truest friends and family, in an increasingly divided wizarding world.</i><br /><br />This book showed me how weak the script of this movie is, and how right I was to not have liked it as much as the previous one. <b>That's all I'm going to say when it comes to the plot of the movie.</b> Moving on.<br /><br />This movie-script-book was how it was supposed to be. Following the steps of the previous one, it really captures the essence of the movie and makes you feel everything as you did when you watched it. Which makes sense, cause the people who worked on the movie worked on this too. At some points, we see some extra feelings and thoughts of the characters we didn't see in the movie which was a nice lil' bonus. <b>I truly wonder what would it be like to read this before having watched the movie.</b> I might try it next time around.<br /><br />Next up, <b>THE ILLUSTRATIONS</b>. As a graphic designer myself, I can't not comment on that. I feel this book was even more extraordinarily beautiful than the previous one. I commend those graphic designers and illustrators, their work is a piece of art. I couldn't stop looking at those marvelous images which enthralled me all the more into the spirit of the book. <b>The Harry Potter industry knows where it's at.</b><br /><br />Lastly, I gotta talk about what bothered me. Nothing relatable to the plot of the movie, of course. <b>WHY WOULD THE NAMES OF THE CHARACTERS HAD TO BE IN CAPS EVERY DAMN TIME?</b> I felt as though the names were being screaming at me every time I read them, and sometimes I would lose focus. Did this happen in the previous movie-script-book? I don't fucking remember. But I have to tell you, it fucking aggravated me this time around. If it did exist in the previous movie-script-book, that means I have changed as a reader and things annoy more easily, apparently. <b>Well, fuck me.</b><br /><br />Overall, these were 2 productive hours of my life. I love this story, these characters, no matter what the plot does, I will always want to watch them and read about them. I'm so happy my favorite franchise continues, no matter what. And... till the next <b>Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them unneeded book</b> K BYE!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2341178084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2341178084" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2341178084?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408711705" href="/book/show/39337278-fantastic-beasts---the-crimes-of-grindelwald">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=plays">plays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2341178084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9988001256334637488">I watched the movie last night, then read the screenplay this morning. I’m going back to watch it again tonight. I guess that means I like it, a lot. <br/><br/>Here's three things that made the story REAL interesting: <br/><br/><b>1. Grindelwald’s leadership</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542278344ra/26601123.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the first time we are really seeing his character. And it’s a little more complex than I supposed. Unlike Voldemort, Grindelwald is not inherently evil and he doesn’t appear to desire power for himself (only the fruition of his vision for the world, a bette</span>
  <span id="freeText9988001256334637488" style="display:none">I watched the movie last night, then read the screenplay this morning. I’m going back to watch it again tonight. I guess that means I like it, a lot. <br><br>Here's three things that made the story REAL interesting: <br><br><b>1. Grindelwald’s leadership</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542278344ra/26601123.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the first time we are really seeing his character. And it’s a little more complex than I supposed. Unlike Voldemort, Grindelwald is not inherently evil and he doesn’t appear to desire power for himself (only the fruition of his vision for the world, a better world.) I wonder where he sees himself in the aftermath? <br><br>He’s also extremely manipulative and can persuade otherwise good characters to follow him (and not out of fear.) They follow him because there is an undercurrent of truth in his ideas. He wants peace for the world, but, of course, the kind of peace he wants could only be bought with blood and death. I’m looking forward to seeing where this goes, to finding out whether he is a hypocrite in his leadership or a genuine visionary (though I think I already know the real answer.) <br><br>The point is, there's more to him than the typical one dimensional villain archetype he was said to be. <br><br><b>2. Young Dumbledore</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542279085ra/26601144.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dumbledore has always been a bit of an enigma. He possesses knowledge and history that we know nothing about, so it’s great to see a bit of his backstory explored. Now we all know how these films will end (with whose victory and defeat.) But I am still genuinely interested in seeing it play out. It won’t be a clean victory for sure. There are quite a few characters in here that aren’t even mentioned in the Harry Potter series. No doubt, there will be a few deaths coming in the next one. <br><br><br><b>3. Nagini as a Maledictus</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542277856ra/26601093.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This for me was one of the most exciting things about the movie because it left me with me so many questions. At one-point Nagini, Voldemort’s pet snake and horcrux, was once a normal girl who felt love and pain and longed for acceptance. She was cursed to forever take the form of snake in later life, but how did she join the side of evil? I’m sure the next film will give us the answers we seek. <br><br><b>Final thoughts</b><br><br>There are some weak points in the movie such as it’s over fixation with Credence and his lineage, but the reveal of exactly who he is at the end kind of makes it all worth it. I must admit, I really did not see that coming!<br><br> Also, a note on the screenplay itself, like the previous one it is just an exact replicate of the movie. There's nothing new here, but I enjoyed reading it nevertheless.<br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sean.barrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>| <a href="https://twitter.com/ultra_vegan" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>| <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sean.ultra_vegan/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Insta</a>| <a href="https://york.academia.edu/SeanBarrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Academia</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9988001256334637488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2556973638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556973638" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2556973638?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338263893" href="/book/show/39331761-fantastic-beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556973638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4670314072213173620"><b>4.5 STARS!</b> if you're wondering where that half a star went, ask Rowling—she probably threw it in the trash with the timeline 😂<blockquote>
  <i>“Regret is my constant companion. Do not let it become yours.”</i>
</blockquote>The second installment in the Fantastic Beasts 5-movie series and a screenplay (not a novel) <b>full of magic!</b><br/><br/>There are reasons I absolutely appreciated this despite what many might say, and reasons I didn't—I'll be responding to some of the criticisms, too, while supporting others.<br/><br/>One thing's clear: while J.K</span>
  <span id="freeText4670314072213173620" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS!</b> if you're wondering where that half a star went, ask Rowling—she probably threw it in the trash with the timeline 😂<blockquote>
  <i>“Regret is my constant companion. Do not let it become yours.”</i>
</blockquote>The second installment in the Fantastic Beasts 5-movie series and a screenplay (not a novel) <b>full of magic!</b><br><br>There are reasons I absolutely appreciated this despite what many might say, and reasons I didn't—I'll be responding to some of the criticisms, too, while supporting others.<br><br>One thing's clear: while J.K. Rowling made some great choices, she also made some mistakes while trying to appeal to the fans; <b>the McGonagall dilemma not even the worst one</b>.<br><br>The thing the whole series seems to hang on to while dangling on the edge of the precipice is what could mess this up—<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AURELIUS CAN'T POSSIBLY BE DUMBLEDORE'S BROTHER. Why? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Read the “<b>Broken Timeline &amp; Theories</b>” section for how the timeline was cracked and how Rowling might fix it. Don't worry about major spoilers, I've hidden those.<blockquote>“Oh, Newt. You never met a monster you couldn’t love.”</blockquote>Anyways, I'm so glad I read the screenplay before watching the movie—because I both got to first imagine it all in my head and also I noticed details and read about characters' thoughts in the book that later helped notice and understand more things from the film! <b>I suggest you try doing the same.</b><br>The book is beautifully designed whatever it is, and I loved the <i>illustrations</i>!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550586119i/27087839._SY540_.jpg" height="161" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550586119i/27087840._SY540_.jpg" height="161" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550586119i/27087841._SY540_.jpg" height="161" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Storyline &amp; Criticisms</b>
</u><br><br><b>1927. New York.</b><br>Grindelwald, held by the <i>Magical Congress of the United States of America</i> (MACUSA), plans to make good on his promise to escape. <b>He has a manipulative tongue and you have no idea who he'd bewitch with his words.</b><blockquote>Newt: It was a field trip. I was collecting material for my book on magical beasts—<br>Travers: You destroyed half of New York.</blockquote><b>London.</b><br>Newt Scamander, now banned from international travel by the British Ministry of Magic after his misadventures the last year, finds himself confronted by none other than <b>Albus Dumbledore, who knows much and reveals little,</b> asking Newt to do what they both believe is right. <b>Even at the expense of breaking the law.</b><blockquote>“I do not fight out of hatred. I say the Muggles are not lesser, but other. Not worthless, but of other value. Not disposable, but of a different disposition.”</blockquote><b>Paris.</b><br>A girl who turns into a snake ... a boy who seeks his family and heritage ... a man with revenge in his heart ... a society of pure-bloods bent on rulling the world—<b>it's a mess that Newt finds himself in the midst of</b>, even if he did everything he could to stay away because he doesn't do sides.<br><br><b>
  <i>On criticisms:</i>
</b> the strange thing is, some say this story had nothing really happening, some say there was too much and too little time. <b>I say it was just right.</b><br><br>I don't care that we know how it's all gonna end as it's a prequel clarifying the the events of the Global Wizarding War.<br><b>But there is so much we don't know about that period and Grindelwald and Dumbledore, with so many characters whose involvements we hadn't learned about!</b><br>I believe this is the best way of exploring that piece of history—it's not like Dumbledore was so forthcoming with Harry or that Harry even had time to give us an explicitly detailed account of the history of the Wizarding World.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550585529ra/27087788.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Characterization &amp; Criticisms</b>
</u><br><br>Newt Scamander is the precious unexpected hero this world has needed; Tina Goldstein the auror I want to see have <b>more of a character development;</b> Jacob Kowalski the much needed No-Maj I can't get enough of; and <b>Pickett the love of my life!</b> Nope, I ain't kidding kiddos :) AND NICOLAS FLAMEL WAS SO ADORABLE.<br><br>Not to forget Albus Dumbledore, the usual anigmatic, secretive man who <b>we get to learn so much more about!</b> My heart <i>breaks</i> for him—I loved seeing this side of him we'd just read about in the last Harry Potter book, <b>and I NEED THE NEXT 3 BOOKS AND FILMS RIGHT NOW.</b><br><br>Now the ones that demand a little more discussion:<br><br><b>
  <i>Queenie Goldstein</i>
</b> is free-spirited, brave, compassionate, desires peace. So I find it not at all illogical she makes the choice she does in <i>Crimes of Grindelwald</i>—<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she believes by helping Grindelwald, they can prevent World War II, and that aligns with her peaceful tendencies.<br><br>Besides, <b>Grindelwald has manipulated her, lied to her, and slowly won ger over by making all that talk of not hating No-Majs and doing this to “allow love to grow”.</b><br><br>No she's not stupid—but she's desperate and Grindelwald a skilled manipulator. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> You might find yourself doing the same thing if you're convinced it's the right choice and will bring freedom!<br><br><br><b>
  <i>Gellert Grindelwald</i>
</b> is one of the main reasons I appreciate this book—because he's <i>not</i> the Voldemort type of villain. Voldemort was brute force and ruled with terror; <b>Grindelwald, though, is the type of villain I enjoy and <i>admire</i></b>, however weird that sounds. I'm usually obsessed with great villains, and do a lot of analysis on them :)<br><br>He's sneaky and subtle, someone who understands the power of words and wields it beautifully. He's more dangerous than Voldemort because you-know-who's followers were mostly there out of fear—and <b>while fear is a notable motivator, it can turn on you just as easily.</b><br><br>Gellert knows that, and so he, with his smart and conniving mind, manipulates people into believing his cause <i>theirs</i>. <b>He is a capable leader and sees right through people, finding what he can twist to make them think assisting him is exactly what they want!</b><br><br>He might seek power, yes (as we learned about his and Dumbledore's past in <i>The Deathly Hallows</i>), but he also <i>believes</i> in his cause with his own kind of logic; and that, my friend—that <b>faith and belief and ill-used reason—is the most dangerous thing of all.</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>Leta Lestrange</i>
</b> is the Sirius Black of the Lestrange family tree. In every sense! I definitely <i>loved</i> her and her backstory was a major strong point of this installment for me and the needy Harry Potter fans who wanna know more about all the great and small families!<br><br>Now, there's this problem being discussed around about Leta, and <b>I really need to clarify something cause it seems people got it wrong</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her death doesn't mean the end of the Lestrange family! I mean, her <i>branch</i> of the family wasn't the last one of<br> them.<br><br><b>I suggest reading this article to understand the family tree and their connection to Rosiers and Blacks and how Bellatrix might come around:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.fandom.com/articles/untangling-the-lestrange-family-tree">https://www.fandom.com/articles/untan...</a><br><br>Besides, the actor Zoë Kravitz said she's Bellatrix's great-great-aunt. So who knows? Maybe she's not dead? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Broken Timeline &amp; Theories</b>
</u><br><br><u>1)</u> First there's the <b>McGonagall dilemma</b>; so what is it?<br><br>The movie is set during 1927, and there's a Leta flashback to when she was 13 and at Hogwarts. Leta was born on September 1896, so she attended Hogwarts from 1908 to 1915 (not 1907, because she would turn 11 when school had already started) making her the same year and classmate of Newt (who was born in 1897).<br>So that means the flashback to 13-year-old Leta was somewhere from September 1909 to September 1910. The flashback was also the last days of winter terms. So of course it's the end of winter of 1909. <b>Why is all this a problem?</b><br><br>Because while Rowling never announced a year for McGonagall's birthday, we know that she began teaching at Hogwarts 2 years after graduating. In <i>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</i>, we discover that McGonagall has been working at Hogwarts for 39 years, meaning she should’ve graduated in 1954.<br>Since in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31539949.Short_Stories_from_Hogwarts_of_Heroism__Hardship_and_Dangerous_Hobbies__Pottermore_Presents___1_" title="Short Stories from Hogwarts of Heroism, Hardship and Dangerous Hobbies (Pottermore Presents, #1) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener"> Short Stories from Hogwarts of Heroism, Hardship and Dangerous Hobbies</a> Rowling confirms her birthday as 4th October, McGonagall was almost 19 years old when she finished Hogwarts, and so her birth year can be inferred as 1935.<br><br>Now, do you get where I'm going? <b>She was born in 1935, but appeared not only in a 1927 story, but TEACHING AS A PROFESSOR AT HOGWARTS IN 1909.</b><br><br>Um, did anyone bother to, like, google her at least before writing this screenplay? No? I thought so.<br><br><b>How can we explain that away?</b> Some wanna think she's a descendant of our McGonagall, but that can't be.<br><br>Because in <i>Short Stories from Hogwarts of Heroism, Hardship and Dangerous Hobbies</i> we learn that McGonagall is the family name of her father, a Scottish Presbyterian minister, who was a Muggle and had had no relations to wizards before.<br><br>Also, we <i>do</i> know that it is our Minerva McGonagall—in the screenplay, she is specifically referred to as “young Minerva McGonagall”, and in a deleted scene in the film, Dumbledore calls her by her first name.<br><br><b>So the only possible way to explain it away is a time turner</b>. But what is so important to risk the use of such fickle magic just to give Minerva the chance to teach years before she was born? I have no idea!<br><br>Mistakes like the days of the week not matching the calendar (with Harry's birthday, for example) are easy enough to ignore—<b>but this? It almost seems impossible for all these people to really not notice such an <i>obvious</i> detail!!</b><br><br>That's not even the worst one.<br><br><u>2) Most important is the <b>CREDENCE DILEMMA</b> the whole series depends on,</u> for which I've got a couple of theories. It's a major spoiler, though:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Here's why the major twist of the story—being Credence's true identity as Aurelius Dumbledore and Albus's brother—can't be true.<br><br>In 1901 during the Atlantic boat crossing flashback, we read that Credence was a baby.<br>Now, Kendra, the Dumbledores' mother, died a while before Ariana, who died in 1899. And Percival, their father, was imprisoned in Azkaban in 1890.<br><br>So a simple math makes us realize that <b>Credence couldn't possibly be born to either of Albus's parents in 1901 or even 1900, when one was dead and another in a prison no one breaks out of until 1982.</b><br><br>Now, the fact that the baby Credence was on a ship bound for America with the Lestrange children means his heritage and reasons for fleeing Europe is a mystery that has to mean something.<br><br><b>That leaves 3 possiblities</b>: either,<br><br><b>a)</b> Grindelwald was lying—which isn't impossible, as he's known to be a sneaky manipulative man that will say anything to get his ends; or<br><br><b>b)</b> he wasn't lying, but Credence isn't <i>really</i> a Dumbledore, it's the Obscurus inside of him that is somehow tied to Ariana, the third Dumbledore—a suspected Obscurus herself, though she died in 1899 during a three-way duel between her brothers and Gellert.<br>Maybe <i>someone</i> saved her Obscurus and then after being preserved (like the one Newt kept) it was given a host in Credence, somehow?<br>It also should be noted that in a deleted scene in <i>Crimes of Grindelwald</i>, Albus tells Newt that Grindelwald is obsessed with Credence because his Seer had a vision that an Obscurus will kill the man he fears the most—one would wonder when he had that vision, exactly ... Or<br><br><b>c)</b> Credence <i>is</i> Albus's brother and we'll be told that Barty Crouch Jr. wasn't, in fact, the first person to escape Azkaban in 1982, or Sirius Black the first person to escape without outside help in 1993—but that Dumbledore's father did too and had a son later who'd be Aurelius. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>We'll just have to wait and see which of these strategies Rowling chooses to explain the Credence dilemma—or maybe she'll do something else entirely! I just hope she gives some sense to it.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>Movie Adaptation</b>
</u><br><br><i>
  <b>Casting &amp; Acting:</b>
</i> There's no doubt acting in a film with this many magical nonexistent creatures is very difficult and will run every actor dry; and I admire Eddie Redmayne (<i>Newt Scamander</i>) because he had it the hardest, having to take care of them and interact with them—<b>I'm just impressed!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550585529ra/27087789.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Katherine Waterston (<i>Tina Goldstein</i>), thankfully did a better job than the she did in the previous film in my opinion, and I'm hopeful for the future!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550591989ra/27088233.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dan Fogler (<i>Jacob Kowalski</i>) was as awe-inspiring as always. Alison Sudol (<i>Queenie Goldstein</i>) managed the new depth of character that Queenie got in this sequel <b>perfectly</b>. And Zoë Kravitz (<i>Leta Lestrange</i>) was the best one for the role!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550591989ra/27088234.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jude Law (<i>Albus Dumbledore</i>) was one of my favourite things! He strangely <b>fit it so well</b> and pulled off Dumbledore's mysterious yet well intentions, his charisma and enigmatic character!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550591989ra/27088235.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Johnny Depp (<i>Gellert Grindelwald</i>) I'm not completely against. <b>Yes, he wouldn't have been my choice, but he was okay. So I can make my peace with it, I guess.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550591989ra/27088236.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>Directing, CGI, etc:</b>
</i> I loved it once again, while maybe the special effects could've been better.<br>The magic was in some places <i>breathtaking</i>, and then sometimes lacking. But mostly it was great :)<br><br><br><u>
  <b>Companions</b>
</u><br><br><i>
  <b>Books in series:</b>
</i><br>• <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29363501.Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_The_Original_Screenplay" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them: The Original Screenplay</a> (Fantastic Beasts The Original Screenplay, #1) [<b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555463085" rel="nofollow noopener">MY REVIEW</a>
</b>]<br><br><i><b>Book playlist:</b><br>(from the motion picture original soundtrack, all instrumental)</i><br>• “Leta’s Theme (Solo Piano)” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Leta’s Flashback” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Salamader Eyes” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Vision of War” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Leta’s Confession” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Newt and Jacob Pack for Paris” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Spread the Word” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Fantastic Beasts Theme (Solo Piano)” by James Newton Howard<br>• “Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Grindelwald” by James Newton Howard<br><br><i>
  <b>Related books:</b>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2368011535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368011535" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368011535?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408711705" href="/book/show/39337278-fantastic-beasts---the-crimes-of-grindelwald">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368011535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11707013791671525782"><b>SPOILERS! SPOILERS! BEWARE ALL YE WHO ENTER HERE!</b> <br/><br/>Ah, well. *shrugs* <i>You've been warned...</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011629.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I’m sorry</b>, dear Newt. I wish that I could agree with you, but…<i>WHAT. WAS. THAT</i>?!!! I’ve never been <b>angry and disappointed</b> at a Harry Potter film before! What on Earth happened? Was J.K. Rowling actually the screenwriter or is this another case of the <i>Cursed Child</i>? <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011630.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let’s start with <b>Queenie</b>, one of my <i>favourite</i> characters. Remember the <b>adorable sweetheart</b> that she was in the first film? Well, sorry! <i>THAT QUEEN</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11707013791671525782" style="display:none"><b>SPOILERS! SPOILERS! BEWARE ALL YE WHO ENTER HERE!</b> <br><br>Ah, well. *shrugs* <i>You've been warned...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011629.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I’m sorry</b>, dear Newt. I wish that I could agree with you, but…<i>WHAT. WAS. THAT</i>?!!! I’ve never been <b>angry and disappointed</b> at a Harry Potter film before! What on Earth happened? Was J.K. Rowling actually the screenwriter or is this another case of the <i>Cursed Child</i>? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011630.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let’s start with <b>Queenie</b>, one of my <i>favourite</i> characters. Remember the <b>adorable sweetheart</b> that she was in the first film? Well, sorry! <i>THAT QUEENIE IS D-E-A-D</i>. It’s like she <b>underwent a lobotomy</b> and completely changed personalities. She starts off the film controlling Jacob via a <i>love potion</i> and in doing so, tries to <b>manipulate him</b> into marriage which makes <i>ZERO SENSE</i>, considering that he was <i>ALREADY IN LOVE WITH HER</i>. Then, when he finds out, she runs and <b>joins Grindelwald</b>?? A known wannabe-tyrant and murderer??? Who hates all Muggles, which <b>includes Jacob</b>??? How on Earth does that even make sense??? Jacob loves her, but he doesn’t want her controlling him. He even chases after her!!! Not that she cares…<i>sigh</i>. But this was only the beginning! Just you wait!<br><br><b>Leta Lestrange</b>…I was so excited to get to know her and…guess what? She’s <b>dead</b>, too! But unlike Queenie, she’s actually dead. Wonderful…<i>NOT</i>! She was <i>SO UNDERUTILISED</i>. I loved the dynamic between <b>her, Newt, and Theseus</b>. I actually <b>preferred her with Newt</b> because I find Tina to be rather boring and tedious, but hey, that’s just me. It’s obviously not a possibility now, considering that J.K. Rowling just threw her character away! This also <i>ended the Lestrange line,</i> so how does Bellatrix Black marry into the family, many years in the future??? I’m <b>so confused</b>! Will she be resurrected??? What is happening?!!! I swear that <b>every female character was treated poorly</b> in this film, with the exception of Tina.<br><br>Why is <b>Nagini</b> now a real person? That’s an unnecessary and random storyline. The ending of the film also <i>came out of nowhere</i>. The <b>phoenix</b>??? <b>Credence</b> is <b>Dumbledore’s long lost brother</b>??? Why then, in the future, do we only hear of Aberforth and Ariana??? Why is Credence <i>never mentioned</i>? While Dumbledore never revealed anything that needed to be discussed (insert eye roll here), Aberforth mentioned Ariana. Why did he neglect to include Credence? There is so much in this film that <i>DOESN’T MAKE ANY SENSE</i>!!! Why, J.K. Rowling? <i>WHY</i>?!!!<br><br>I feel like this film wanted to <b>do too much</b> in <b>too little time</b>. They tried to scrunch in <b>so much backstory</b> to propel the plot forward…which was to the detriment of the film. You can’t develop that many characters at once unless you <i>extend the runtime</i> to four or five hours, rather than the two and a half it was given. J.K. Rowling tried to thread together all of the characters <b>at once</b>, which made me not care about any of them. And, why would I? I <i>didn’t have any time</i> to attach myself to them and become sensitive to their backgrounds before a new backstory was thrown at me!<br><br>Also…my girl, <b>Minerva McGonagall</b>, is a professor in this film…despite <b>not being born yet</b>?!!! The film takes place in <b>1927</b>…but Minerva was born in <b>1935</b>! There’s <i>no possible way</i> that she could’ve been teaching <i>before she was even conceived</i>. Was this plain and simple fan service??? I’m certain that J.K. Rowling shall find some way to explain this mistake away. Oh! And Dumbledore, despite being a <b>Transfiguration</b> professor, was teaching <b>Defence Against the Dark Arts</b>??? What the heck is going on here??! It’s like J.K. Rowling <b>doesn’t even care</b> about sticking to the canon of her own world that <i>SHE CREATED</i>! Man, am I disappointed…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011631.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the one thing that I <b>really enjoyed</b> was <b>Jude Law’s portrayal</b> of <b>Albus Dumbledore</b>! He was <i>so suave and charismatic</i>! And in true Dumbledore fashion, he managed to get everyone to <i>do his work for him</i>, despite not divulging <b>any important information to anyone</b> beforehand (Yes, I’m spilling that tea!). While I mentioned not enjoying the casting of Johnny Depp as Gellert Grindelwald in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282209654" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> of the previous film, Jude Law is <i>PERFECT</i> as Albus Dumbledore. I’ve loved this casting choice since the <i>very moment</i> it was announced.<br><br>While I <b>enjoyed this film</b> as a whole because I tend to love anything Harry Potter-related, no matter what, I really hope that J.K. Rowling <b>turns this series around</b> in the next film, or it might be time for me to <b>part ways</b> with the <i>Fantastic Beasts</i> franchise before it <b>ruins all of the love</b> that I have for the <i>Harry Potter</i> series. <br><br>Even though I <b>dislike Snape</b> as a character…his facial expression <i>depicts my feelings</i> about this film perfectly:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549247570ra/27011632.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11707013791671525782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2334403153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2334403153" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2334403153?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338263893" href="/book/show/39331761-fantastic-beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2334403153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7817625549289814820">What the fuck even was that.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542515530ra/26613929.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I haven't watched the movie yet so this is solely a review of the book, but wow, I'm certainly not rushing to the theatres anytime soon.<br/><br/>The story is seriously a big hot mess though and while I loved the first installment, the follow-up really threw everything I liked about it into a blender. The characters changed in ludicrous fashion, the motivations behind the characters themselves were murky at best, and there was little to no plot development. This feels like the </span>
  <span id="freeText7817625549289814820" style="display:none">What the fuck even was that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542515530ra/26613929.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I haven't watched the movie yet so this is solely a review of the book, but wow, I'm certainly not rushing to the theatres anytime soon.<br><br>The story is seriously a big hot mess though and while I loved the first installment, the follow-up really threw everything I liked about it into a blender. The characters changed in ludicrous fashion, the motivations behind the characters themselves were murky at best, and there was little to no plot development. This feels like the middle book of a trilogy but apparently, we have <b>three more books</b> to "look forward to."<br><br>The biggest issue I had was the very clear attempt to merge these "prequel" stories with the original Harry Potter series. I felt if the writers simply focused on telling these stories and letting them stand on their own merits they might not have felt the need to remind us every so often that hey! This is set in the Harry Potter world! It just felt messy. The biggest flaw was McGonagall's cameo. She was in her 70s in the original stories, which began in 1997, yet in The Crimes of Grindewald she's a Hogwarts professor in a story set in the mid-20s. I can imagine the cameos are far more exciting in film, but the timeline super doesn't match, at least in accordance with what Rowling has stated previously about her characters. Seriously, so unnecessary. <br><br>There are also additions to the story that simply don't end up making a whole lot of sense. Like that bit about Nagini having been an actual human at one point in her life? It's revealed that she's a Maledictus, able to transform into a snake but due to a blood curse passed down in her family, she'll transform into a snake one day and never be able to transform back. Sure, it was interesting tidbits and expands on Nagini's story, and sure, maybe this all becomes more vital later on in this series, but the small bit we're given seemed pretty inconsequential.<br><br>But the icing on the cake was the "twist" at the end. Serious spoiler, beware. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[All of a sudden Dumbledore has a long, lost, and apparently dead, but maybe not, brother that has never, ever been mentioned. But of course, it's a brother that he never even knew existed. Bah. I just don't really care, because we've already had enough about Dumbledore. I want more focus on who the central character should be: Newt. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The original stories are already so fascinatingly complex and these attempts to expand on what has already been drilled into our brains from many a re-reads just comes across as lazy and is really destroying the magic of Harry Potter for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542516206ra/26613940.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7817625549289814820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2669325039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669325039" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669325039?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781338263893" href="/book/show/39331761-fantastic-beasts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669325039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18283779729195577066"><b>
  <u>Unexpected developments!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This is the original screenplay used for the film "Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Grindelwald". Which is the second movie in the saga, a prequel saga for the Wizarding World of Harry Potter.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>RETURN TO EUROPE</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Oh, Newt. You never met a monster you couldn't love.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The previous adventure takes the audience to America, to boldly go where no wizard or muggle had gone before, but in this second story, the action takes us back to the old continent, Europe, to visit Engla</span>
  <span id="freeText18283779729195577066" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Unexpected developments!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This is the original screenplay used for the film "Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Grindelwald". Which is the second movie in the saga, a prequel saga for the Wizarding World of Harry Potter.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>RETURN TO EUROPE</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Oh, Newt. You never met a monster you couldn't love.</i>
</b><br /><br />The previous adventure takes the audience to America, to boldly go where no wizard or muggle had gone before, but in this second story, the action takes us back to the old continent, Europe, to visit England first and later remains on France for the rest of the narrative.<br /><br />Reading the book, after watching the movie was a rewarding experience since it solved three small doubts that left me the film (for not going into the big doubts!), but at least the book can explain who was the Chupacabra that exists on Funko Pop, and I didn't notice on the movie, but more precisely, I did notice it, but I didn't know that that creature was the Chupacabra, it was the magical animal with Grindelwald at the beginning; later, I understood why Newt and Grimsson were so uneasy with each other, since Grimmson is a hunter of magical creatures (most likely a furtive one); and finally, it wasn't clear if Non-Magical Parisians were watching the large display of Grindelwald to tell about his reunion, and the book indicated that it was invisible to normal humans (I guessed that it was so, but nothing in the movie was telling me about it).<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Mr. Scamander. Do you think Dumbledore will mourn for you?</i>
</b><br /><br />Certainly, there are some (big) incongruencies to previous historical facts in the <i>Wizarding World of Harry Potter</i>, and I am not forgiving them, but I guess that like in <i>Star Wars</i>, now this pop culture franchise, got into the area of contradict itself from a movie to another.<br /><br />There are characters that they played major roles in the first adventure, while here it looked like J.K. Rowling didn't know what to do with them, now that the saga is taking its long-game path, but I trust that in the following movies (five in total will be), each character will prove his/her worth to the enrichment and impact of the prequel saga. Because, after all, I consider that some characters took paths in this second story that some character in the previous saga never took, since maybe J.K. Rowling got too attached to them, and maybe in this prequel she is taking harsher choices, but indeed brave ones that they will make the whole saga, more interesting and unpredictable.<br /><br />And after all, <i>always</i> is a delightful experience to enjoy a new journey by J.K. Rowling through the <i>Wizarding World of Harry Potter</i>.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18283779729195577066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2910284385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2910284385" />

<span id="freeTextContainer4644184354680975454">I saw the movie last week and knew I had to read the screenplay.<br/>My thoughts are basically the same of the movie. I love Newt Scamander, he's a very interesting and unique character and every time he has a scene I'm happy. I really enjoyed the new characters that were introduced in the story, like for example Leta, Theseus and Nagini.   <span id="freeText4644184354680975454" style="display:none">I saw the movie last week and knew I had to read the screenplay.<br />My thoughts are basically the same of the movie. I love Newt Scamander, he's a very interesting and unique character and every time he has a scene I'm happy. I really enjoyed the new characters that were introduced in the story, like for example Leta, Theseus and Nagini. I just think that the Nagini storyline is unnecessary but we'll see how it's developed in the future. <br />I'm really interested in Grindelwald and Dumbledore's past and I wish they would have shown us more of that, hopefully we'll get more in the next movies/books. <br />Something I truly did not like was the big reveal at the end. It does not make any sense and I really don't know what they're trying to do. </span>

<div id="review_2790056845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2790056845" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2790056845?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2790056845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11761775262641053898"><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This is a sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29363501.Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_The_Original_Screenplay' title='Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them: The Original Screenplay</a>, and picks up where that story ends - with the arrest of Gellert Grindelwald in New York City. Grindelwald is a dark wizard who wants magic folk to rule the world.....and is actively trying to foment a war to make that happen.<br/><br/>*****<br/> <br/>As <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39330961.Fantastic_Beasts_The_Crimes_of_Grindelwald___The_Original_Screenplay' title='Fantastic Beasts The Crimes of Grindelwald - The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Grindelwald - The Original Screenplay</a> opens, the dark wizard is about to be extradited to London to stand trial, escorted by an array of po</span>
  <span id="freeText11761775262641053898" style="display:none"><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>This is a sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29363501.Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_The_Original_Screenplay" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them: The Original Screenplay</a>, and picks up where that story ends - with the arrest of Gellert Grindelwald in New York City. Grindelwald is a dark wizard who wants magic folk to rule the world.....and is actively trying to foment a war to make that happen.<br><br>*****<br> <br>As <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39330961.Fantastic_Beasts_The_Crimes_of_Grindelwald___The_Original_Screenplay" title="Fantastic Beasts The Crimes of Grindelwald - The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantastic Beasts: The Crimes of Grindelwald - The Original Screenplay</a> opens, the dark wizard is about to be extradited to London to stand trial, escorted by an array of powerful aurors. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378094.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Grindelwald is being sent to London</b><br><br>Grindelwald is a wily fellow though, and engineers a clever escape. <br><br>Skip ahead a few months and Grindelwald is in Paris, searching for Credence Barebone, a young, uniquely gifted dark wizard. Grindelwald plans to use Credence to usurp power for wizard-kind, after which muggles will be eliminated or enslaved.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378095.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Grindelwald in Paris</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378096.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Credence Barebone</b><br><br>England's Ministry of Magic wants to kill Credence before he joins forces with Grindelwald, and asks Newt Scamander to help his brother Theseus (an auror) do the job. Newt - who abhors violence - declines, so the Ministry sends other aurors, including Tina Goldstein. Once she's in Paris, Tina learns that a man named Yusuf Kama is also after Credence, and the two hunters join forces.....for different reasons. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378097.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Newt Scamander</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378098.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Theseus Scamander</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378099.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Tina Goldstein</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378100.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Yusuf Kama</b><br><br>Meanwhile Albus Dumbledore sends Newt to Paris (against Ministry orders) to try to 'turn' Credence to the light. Newt is joined by his compadre from the first screenplay, Jacob Kowalski (the muggle baker)….who's in a relationship with Queenie Goldstein (Tina Goldstein's sister). To add to the fun Newt and Tina might be on the cusp of romance, but they're now on opposite sides of the Credence dilemma. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378101.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Young Albus Dumbledore</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378102.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Jacob Kowalski</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378103.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Queenie Goldstein</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378104.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Newt with Tina Goldstein</b><br><br>Dumbledore is repeatedly asked to kill Grindelwald himself, but always says he can't do it. (Potter fans know Grindelwald and Dumbledore were close friends as teens, so this isn't a complete shock.)<br><br>All manner of shenanigans follow, including: a huge wild beast running around Paris; romantic misunderstandings; use of the Avada Kedavra curse; flashbacks to Hogwarts decades ago; visits to the French Ministry of Magic; secrets being exposed; etc. <br><br>Additional characters that make an appearance include Leta Lestrange - who's engaged to Theseus Scamander; (OMG!! Marrying a Lestrange); Nagini - who happens to be a circus freak at this time; and various dark wizards who are enthralled with Grindelwald.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378105.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Leta Lestrange</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555547302i/27378106.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Nagini</b><br><br>This is a rather slight story with a cliffhanger ending, clearly meant to set the stage for future screenplays (and movies) in the series. This book is not as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29363501.Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_The_Original_Screenplay" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them The Original Screenplay by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them: The Original Screenplay</a>.....but it takes place in the Potterverse, so it's worth reading if you're a fan. <br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11761775262641053898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
